                  <foreign lang="ar">أَسِنَّتَهَا</foreign>, [expl. as] meaning <hi rend="ital">When ye journey in the land abounding with herbage, enable ye the ridden beasts to take of the pasturage:</hi> (S, L:) but Az states that A'Obeyd says, I know not <foreign lang="ar">أَسِنَّة</foreign> except as pl. of the <foreign lang="ar">سِنَان</foreign> of the spear; and if the trad. be [correctly] preserved in memory, it seems to be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْنَان</foreign>; for <foreign lang="ar">سِنٌّ</foreign> [sometimes] signifies the [<hi rend="ital">portion of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">herbage upon which camels pasture;</hi> and its pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَسْنَانٌ</foreign>; one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَسْنَانٌ مِنَ المَرْعَى</foreign>; and the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْنَانٌ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">أَسِنَّةٌ</foreign>: Aboo-Sa'eed says that this last is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سِنَانٌ</foreign>, not of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْنَانٌ</foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20845-2" target="سِنَانٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20854"/></foreign> is applied to the [plants, or trees, called] <foreign lang="ar">حَمْض</foreign>, as meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">a strengthener</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">a sharpener of the appetite</hi>] of the camels for the [plants, or trees, called] <foreign lang="ar">خُلَّة</foreign>: [see a phrase in the earlier part of the first paragraph:] in like manner, also, [he says,] when they light upon what is termed <foreign lang="ar">سِنٌّ مِنَ المَرْعَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">a portion of pasturage</hi>], this is termed <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20845-3" target="سِنَانٌ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n20854"/>عَلَى السَّيْرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">a strengthener,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sharpener, for journeying</hi>]: this explanation is approved by Az, and likewise that of A'Obeyd: it is also related, on the authority of Fr, that <foreign lang="ar">السِّنُّ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">the eating vehemently:</hi> [a signification mentioned in the K as well as in the L:] and Az says, I have heard more than one of the Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">أَصَابَتِ الإِبِلُ اليَوْمَ سِنًّا مِنَ المَرْعَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The camels have obtained to-day a good portion of pasturage</hi>] when they have eaten well of the best of the pasturage: Z says that   
      <foreign lang="ar">أَعْطُوا الرُّكُبَ <ref cref="n20845-4" target="أَسِنَّتَهَا" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Give ye to the ridden beasts what will prevent their being slaughtered;</hi> for when their owner pastures them well, they become fat, and goodly in his eye, and therefore he withholds himself, with niggardliness, from slaughtering them, and this [condition of them] is likened to <foreign lang="ar">أَسِنَّة</foreign> [as meaning “ spear-heads ”] pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سِنَانٌ</foreign>: [see also <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذَتْ رِمَاحَهَا</foreign>, said of camels, voce <foreign lang="ar">رُمْحٌ</foreign>:] or if the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سِنٌّ</foreign> be intended by it, the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">enable ye them</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">the ridden beasts</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to take of the pasturage;</hi> and hence the trad., <foreign lang="ar">أَعْطُوا السِّنَّ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">A way, course, rule, mode,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">manner, of acting</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conduct</hi> or <hi rend="ital">life</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">طَرِيقَةٌ</foreign>, (Mgh, L, Msb,) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20847-1" target="سَنَنٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20849"/></foreign>, (S, L,) and <foreign lang="ar">سِيرَةٌ</foreign>; (S, M, L, Msb, K;) whence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">سُنُّوا بِهِمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّةَ أَهْلِ الكِتَابِ</foreign>, expl. in the first paragraph of this art., last sentence but one, (Mgh,) and the saying of the Hudhalee [Khálid Ibn-Zuheyr] cited in the first paragraph of art. <foreign lang="ar">سير</foreign>; (S;) and this is [said to be] the primary signification; (L;) whether <hi rend="ital">good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">bad;</hi> (M, L;) <hi rend="ital">approved</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disapproved:</hi> (Msb:) or, accord. to Sh, <hi rend="ital">a way</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of acting</hi> &amp;c.] <hi rend="ital">that has been instituted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pursued, by former people, and has become one pursued by those after them;</hi> and this, he says, is the primary signification: (L:) it signifies also [particularly] <hi rend="ital">a way of acting</hi> &amp;c. <hi rend="ital">that is commended,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">approved, and right;</hi> wherefore one says, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one is of the people of the commended and right way of acting</hi> &amp;c.; generally meaning, <hi rend="ital">of those who follow the institutes,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ways, of the Prophet</hi>]; and is from   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20847-2" target="سَنَنٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20849"/></foreign> signifying “ a way, ” or “ road; ” (T, L;) and is also <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَنَنٌ</foreign>: (L:) and [the <hi rend="ital">laws,</hi> i. e] the <hi rend="ital">statutes,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ordinances,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">commands and prohibitions,</hi> of God: (Lh, M, L, K:) [also <hi rend="ital">a practice or saying,</hi> or the <hi rend="ital">practices and sayings collectively, of Mohammad, or any other person who is an authority in matters of religion, namely, any prophet, or a Companion of Mohammad,</hi> (see Kull p. 203,) <hi rend="ital">as handed down by tradition:</hi>] when used unrestrictedly in matters of the law, <foreign lang="ar">السُّنَّةُ</foreign> means only <hi rend="ital">what the Prophet</hi> [<hi rend="ital">Mohammad</hi>] <hi rend="ital">has commanded, and what has been handed down from him by tradition,</hi> [or, as in the JM, <hi rend="ital">and what he forbade,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and what he has invited to do, by word or deed, of such things as are not mentioned in the Kur-án;</hi> wherefore one says, in speaking of the directions, or evidences, of the law, <foreign lang="ar">الكِتَابُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَالسُّنَّةُ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">the Kur-án and the Traditions:</hi> (L:) [thus used, it may be rendered <hi rend="ital">the institutes of the Prophet;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his rule</hi> or <hi rend="ital">usage:</hi>] or in the law it signifies <hi rend="ital">the way of acting</hi> &amp;c. <hi rend="ital">that is pursued in religion without being made obligatory,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">necessary;</hi> it is <hi rend="ital">what the Prophet persevered in doing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">observing, with omitting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">neglecting,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">it</hi>] <hi rend="ital">sometimes; and if the said persevering is in the way of religious service, it constitutes</hi> [<hi rend="ital">what are termed</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">سُنَنُ الهُدَى</foreign>; <hi rend="ital">if in the way of custom,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُنَنُ الزَّوَائِدِ</foreign>: <hi rend="ital">so that</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّةُ الهُدَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of right direction</hi>] <hi rend="ital">is that of which the observance is a completion of religion, and it is that to the omission,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">neglect, whereof attach blame and misdemeanour; and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّةُ الزَّوَائِدِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of supererogatory acts</hi>] <hi rend="ital">is that of which the observance is good, but to the omission,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">neglect, whereof neither blame nor misdemeanour attaches, such as the ways of the Prophet in his standing and sitting and clothing and eating:</hi> (KT:) <foreign lang="ar">سُنَنٌ</foreign> is the pl. (Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّةُ الأَوَّلِينَ</foreign>, in the Kur xviii. 53, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">سُنَّتُنَا فِى الأَوَّلِينَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The way pursued by us in respect of the former,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">preceding peoples</hi>], means the destruction decreed to befall them; (Jel;) or extirpation; (Bd;) or, as Zj says, their beholding punishment; (<foreign lang="ar">أَنَّهُمْ عَايَنُوا العَذَابَ</foreign>; [or, as expl. in the K, <foreign lang="ar">مُعَايَنَةُ العَذَابِ</foreign>;]) for the believers in a plurality of gods said, [as is related in the Kur viii. 32,] O God, if this be the truth from Thee, then do Thou rain down upon us stones from heaven. (M, L.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">Nature; natural,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">native, disposition, temper,</hi> or other <hi rend="ital">quality</hi> or <hi rend="ital">property:</hi> (M, L, K:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">سُنَنٌ</foreign>. (M, L.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And The <hi rend="ital">face;</hi> (M, L, K;) because of its polish and smoothness: (M, L:) or the <hi rend="ital">ball of the cheek</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">حُرُّ الوَجْهِ</foreign>): or the <hi rend="ital">circuit</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">دَائِرَة</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of the face:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the form:</hi> (M, L, K:) or the <hi rend="ital">form</hi> of the face: (S:) or the <hi rend="ital">forehead and two sides thereof:</hi> (M, L, K:) all from the meaning of polish and smoothness and evenness: (M, L:) or the <hi rend="ital">principal part</hi> of the face; the <hi rend="ital">part</hi> thereof <hi rend="ital">in which beauty is generally known to lie:</hi> (M in art. <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign>:) or the <hi rend="ital">side</hi> of the cheek: pl. <foreign lang="ar">سُنَنٌ</foreign>. (L.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ قَبَِيحُ السُّنَّةِ</foreign>

                  <form>

                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is said to mean <hi rend="ital">The place of the running of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَرَاب</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">mirage,</hi> app. <hi rend="ital">in consequence of the hot wind</hi>]: or <hi rend="ital">the place of the vehement heat of the hot wind;</hi> as though it were running to and fro therein (<foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّهَا تَسْتَنُّ فِيهِ عَدْوًا</foreign>): or it may mean <hi rend="ital">the place whence issues the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">hot</hi>] <hi rend="ital">wind:</hi> but the first is the explanation given by the preceding authorities. (M, L.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">المُسْتَنُّ</foreign> [an epithet used as meaning] <hi rend="ital">The lion.</hi> (K. [Thus applied, act. part. n. of <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتَنَّ</foreign>.])
